initiated from a 1:1 chat (e.g. agent sending an Adaptive Card via the `send` tool) may be delivered to the channel conversation instead.\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nFor DMs, the inbound context sets `To` as `user:{aadObjectId}` (not `conversation:{conversationId}`). When the `send` tool resolves the target via `findByUserId` in `conversation-store-fs.ts`, it returns the **first** matching conversation for that user — which may be a channel or group chat rather than the originating 1:1 conversation.\\n\\n`findByUserId` iterates `Object.entries()` on the conversation store JSON and returns the first match with no recency or conversation-type awareness.\\n\\n## Possible Fixes\\n\\n1. **Track recency**: Add an `updatedAt` timestamp to stored conversation references and have `findByUserId` return the most recently active conversation.\\n2. **Use conversation ID for DMs**: Change the `To` value for DMs from `user:{senderId}` to `conversation:{conversationId}` so `resolveMSTeamsSendContext` does an exact conversation lookup instead of a user-based search.\\n3. **Pass originating conversation through**: Have the agent's `send` tool inherit the originating conversation ID from the session context rather than resolving by user.\\n\\n## Reproduction\\n\\n1. initiated from a 1:1 chat (e.g. agent sending an Adaptive Card via the `send` tool) may be delivered to the channel conversation instead.\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nFor DMs, the inbound context sets `To` as `user:{aadObjectId}` (not `conversation:{conversationId}`). When the `send` tool resolves the target via `findByUserId` in `conversation-store-fs.ts`, it returns the **first** matching conversation for that user — which may be a channel or group chat rather than the originating 1:1 conversation.\\n\\n`findByUserId` iterates `Object.entries()` on the conversation store JSON and returns the first match with no recency or conversation-type awareness.\\n\\n## Possible Fixes\\n\\n1. **Track recency**: Add an `updatedAt` timestamp to stored conversation references and have `findByUserId` return the most recently active conversation.\\n2. **Use conversation ID for DMs**: Change the `To` value for DMs from `user:{senderId}` to `conversation:{conversationId}` so `resolveMSTeamsSendContext` does an exact conversation lookup instead of a user-based search.\\n3. **Pass originating conversation through**: Have the agent's `send` tool inherit the originating conversation ID from the session context rather than resolving by user.\\n\\n## Reproduction\\n\\n1. The gateway reports success (`BlueBubbles webhook listening`) even when the plugin failed\\n2. The config validation error is logged only to stderr, not surfaced in the gateway status\\n3. The 404 looks identical to a routing bug, not a config bug\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Set `channels.bluebubbles.dmPolicy = \\\"open\\\"` without setting `allowFrom: [\\\"*\\\"]`\\n2. Restart the gateway\\n3. POST to `/bluebubbles-webhook` → 404\\n4. Check logs: `Invalid config: channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom: channels.bluebubbles.dmPolicy=\\\"open\\\" requires channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom to include \\\"*\\\"`\\n5. Meanwhile gateway logs: `[default] BlueBubbles webhook listening on /bluebubbles-webhook` ← **misleading**\\n\\n## Debugging Journey (what makes this P0)\\n\\nSpent 3+ hours investigating this thinking it was a routing bug:\\n- Confirmed gateway was running ✅\\n- Confirmed BB webhook registered in logs ✅  \\n- Confirmed BB was receiving messages ✅\\n- POSTed directly to webhook endpoint → HTTP 404 ❌\\n- Rolled back from 2026.3.13 → 2026.3.1 (no change)\\n- Patched gateway-cli source files directly (no effect — wrong diagnosis)\\n- Restarted gateway 20+ times\\n- Full Mac reboot\\n- Inspected Node ESM module loading, registry singletons, canvas static server routing\\n\\nRoot cause was finally found by grepping for \\\"Invalid config\\\" in gateway.err.log.\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\n1. **Gateway should refuse to start** (or at minimum log a prominent ERROR) if config validation fails for a channel — not log \\\"webhook listening\\\" and silently drop all inbound traffic\\n2. The invalid config error should appear in `openclaw gateway status` output\\n3. `openclaw doctor` should catch this and flag it as a blocking error\\n\\n## Actual Behavior\\n\\n- Gateway starts and reports healthy\\n- `BlueBubbles webhook listening` logged (misleading — route not actually registered)  \\n- All POST /bluebubbles-webhook → 404\\n- Config error buried in stderr: `Invalid config at openclaw.json: channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom: channels.bluebubbles.dmPolicy=\\\"open\\\" requires channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom to include \\\"*\\\"`\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nSet `dmPolicy` to `\\\"allowlist\\\"` (uses `allowFrom` list without full open access) or `\\\"pairing\\\"` (requires handshake). Do **not** use `\\\"open\\\"` unless `allowFrom` contains `\\\"*\\\"`.\\n\\nThe real fix needed from OpenClaw: **fail loudly when channel config is invalid**, don't silently skip plugin initialization.\\n\\n## Environment\\n\\n- OpenClaw: 2026.3.13\\n- macOS 26.3.0 (Darwin arm64)\\n- BlueBubbles: 1.9.9 with Private API enabled\\n- Node: 25.6.1\\n\\n## Impact\\n\\n- **Complete loss of BlueBubbles/iMessage inbound** with no obvious error\\n- Extremely difficult to diagnose — looks like a gateway HTTP routing bug\\n- Affects anyone who accidentally sets an invalid dmPolicy (e.g. The gateway reports success (`BlueBubbles webhook listening`) even when the plugin failed\\n2. The config validation error is logged only to stderr, not surfaced in the gateway status\\n3. The 404 looks identical to a routing bug, not a config bug\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Set `channels.bluebubbles.dmPolicy = \\\"open\\\"` without setting `allowFrom: [\\\"*\\\"]`\\n2. Restart the gateway\\n3. POST to `/bluebubbles-webhook` → 404\\n4. Check logs: `Invalid config: channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom: channels.bluebubbles.dmPolicy=\\\"open\\\" requires channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom to include \\\"*\\\"`\\n5. Meanwhile gateway logs: `[default] BlueBubbles webhook listening on /bluebubbles-webhook` ← **misleading**\\n\\n## Debugging Journey (what makes this P0)\\n\\nSpent 3+ hours investigating this thinking it was a routing bug:\\n- Confirmed gateway was running ✅\\n- Confirmed BB webhook registered in logs ✅  \\n- Confirmed BB was receiving messages ✅\\n- POSTed directly to webhook endpoint → HTTP 404 ❌\\n- Rolled back from 2026.3.13 → 2026.3.1 (no change)\\n- Patched gateway-cli source files directly (no effect — wrong diagnosis)\\n- Restarted gateway 20+ times\\n- Full Mac reboot\\n- Inspected Node ESM module loading, registry singletons, canvas static server routing\\n\\nRoot cause was finally found by grepping for \\\"Invalid config\\\" in gateway.err.log.\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\n1. **Gateway should refuse to start** (or at minimum log a prominent ERROR) if config validation fails for a channel — not log \\\"webhook listening\\\" and silently drop all inbound traffic\\n2. The invalid config error should appear in `openclaw gateway status` output\\n3. `openclaw doctor` should catch this and flag it as a blocking error\\n\\n## Actual Behavior\\n\\n- Gateway starts and reports healthy\\n- `BlueBubbles webhook listening` logged (misleading — route not actually registered)  \\n- All POST /bluebubbles-webhook → 404\\n- Config error buried in stderr: `Invalid config at openclaw.json: channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom: channels.bluebubbles.dmPolicy=\\\"open\\\" requires channels.bluebubbles.allowFrom to include \\\"*\\\"`\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nSet `dmPolicy` to `\\\"allowlist\\\"` (uses `allowFrom` list without full open access) or `\\\"pairing\\\"` (requires handshake). Do **not** use `\\\"open\\\"` unless `allowFrom` contains `\\\"*\\\"`.\\n\\nThe real fix needed from OpenClaw: **fail loudly when channel config is invalid**, don't silently skip plugin initialization.\\n\\n## Environment\\n\\n- OpenClaw: 2026.3.13\\n- macOS 26.3.0 (Darwin arm64)\\n- BlueBubbles: 1.9.9 with Private API enabled\\n- Node: 25.6.1\\n\\n## Impact\\n\\n- **Complete loss of Content\\n\\n### Problem Description\\n\\nOpenClaw fails to accurately track token usage due to mismatched field names between expected and actual API responses, causing context usage to display as `0/80k (0%)` even when the model is actively consuming significant tokens.\\n\\n**Environment:**\\n- 🦞 OpenClaw: 2026.3.23-1\\n- 🧠 Model: llama-cpp/qwen35b-local\\n- 📚 Context Display: 0/80k (0%)\\n- local deployment solution |\\n| ❌ **Ollama** | AFFECTED | Popular model management service |\\n| ✅ **vLLM** | NOT AFFECTED | Compatible (OpenAI format) |\\n| ✅ **HuggingFace TGI** | NOT AFFECTED | Compatible (OpenAI format) |\\n| ✅ **OpenAI API** | NOT AFFECTED | Compatible (OpenAI format) |\\n\\n### Root Cause\\n\\nOpenClaw expects these field names at line ~181675:\\n\\n```javascript\\ninput: response.usage?.input_tokens ?? 0,\\noutput: response.usage?.output_tokens ?? 0,\\n```\\n\\nHowever, different frameworks return different field names:\\n\\n#### llama.cpp server (OpenAI-compatible format)\\n```json\\n{\\n  \\\"usage\\\": {\\n    \\\"prompt_tokens\\\": 11,\\n    \\\"completion_tokens\\\": 1,\\n    \\\"total_tokens\\\": 12\\n  }\\n}\\n```\\n\\n#### Ollama (custom format)\\n```json\\n{\\n  \\\"prompt_eval_count\\\": 26,\\n  \\\"eval_count\\\": 259\\n}\\n```\\n\\n#### vLLM / TGI / OpenAI (OpenAI standard format)\\n```json\\n{\\n  \\\"usage\\\": {\\n    \\\"prompt_tokens\\\": 100,\\n    \\\"completion_tokens\\\": 50,\\n    \\\"total_tokens\\\": 150\\n  }\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### Real-World Case\\n\\n**User Configuration:**\\n- OpenClaw Display: `0/80k (0%)`\\n- Remote llama-server (192.168.3.77:8080) Actual Usage: `43250/80000 (54%)`\\n\\n**Cause:** llama.cpp server returns `prompt_tokens`, but OpenClaw expects `input_tokens`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Chain Reactions from Failed Context Statistics\\n\\n### 1. Context Window Overflow Risk\\n\\n**Due to inability to accurately track token usage:**\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n1. User cannot see real-time token usage rate\\n2. Cannot determine if conversation is approaching the 80k context limit\\n3. May lead to:\\n   - **Model truncation:** Ultra-long conversations are forcibly truncated\\n   - **Quality degradation:** Context overflow causes model to forget early conversation\\n   - **Session crash:** API returns errors after exceeding limits\\n\\n**Actual Impact:**\\n- In long conversation scenarios, users may encounter context overflow without warning\\n- Important conversation content may be lost\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 2. Conversation Management Failure\\n\\nOpenClaw's conversation management mechanisms rely on accurate token counting:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Auto-compression mechanism fails:**\\n   - OpenClaw may decide to compress historical messages based on token usage rate\\n   - If count is 0, compression never triggers\\n   - Leads to unlimited accumulation of historical messages, eventually causing memory overflow\\n\\n2. **Session reset strategy fails:**\\n   - Under some configurations, sessions automatically reset when token usage reaches a threshold\\n   - Due to count being 0, reset never triggers\\n   - Leads to uncontrolled session length\\n\\n3. **Resource waste:**\\n   - Cannot accurately evaluate token cost per session\\n   - May lead to unnecessary long conversations\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 3. Cost Monitoring Failure\\n\\nEven with free local models, token statistics are important performance metrics:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Performance analysis difficulty:**\\n   - Cannot analyze token consumption across different conversations\\n   - Cannot identify abnormally high token usage patterns\\n   - Difficult to optimize conversation strategies\\n\\n2. **Multi-model comparison fails:**\\n   - If multiple model backends exist, cannot fairly compare token efficiency\\n   - Cannot make model switching decisions based on token usage\\n\\n3. **API quota monitoring fails** (if using paid APIs):\\n   - Cannot accurately track API quota usage\\n   - May unexpectedly exceed quota causing service interruption\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 4. LCM (Lossless Context Management) Function Abnormalities\\n\\nOpenClaw's LCM system relies on token statistics to manage conversation history:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Historical message compression strategy fails:**\\n   - LCM decides whether to compress history based on token usage rate\\n   - When count is 0, compression never triggers\\n   - Leads to uncontrolled memory usage\\n\\n2. **Context optimization fails:**\\n   - LCM cannot intelligently retain important conversations\\n   - May lead to important information being discarded too early\\n\\n3. **Search and retrieval functionality affected:**\\n   - LCM's search function may rely on token statistics\\n   - Leads to inaccurate search results\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 5. User Experience Degradation\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **User confusion:**\\n   - See `0/80k (0%)` display\\n   - User cannot determine conversation status\\n   - May mistakenly think system is malfunctioning\\n\\n2. **Trust reduction:**\\n   - Key metrics display incorrectly\\n   - User may question the reliability of the entire system\\n\\n3. **Cannot optimize conversation strategy:**\\n   - User cannot adjust conversation methods based on token usage\\n   - Cannot learn how to efficiently use the context window\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 6. Diagnosis and Debugging Difficulty\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Problem troubleshooting difficulty:**\\n   - If conversation anomalies occur, cannot locate issues through token statistics\\n   - Increases troubleshooting time costs\\n\\n2. **Performance optimization blocked:**\\n   - Cannot perform performance optimization based on token statistics\\n   - Difficult to identify performance bottlenecks\\n\\n3. **Automated testing fails:**\\n   - Automated tests may rely on token statistics as success metrics\\n   - Leads to inaccurate test results\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 7. Resource Allocation Issues in Multi-User/Multi-Session Scenarios\\n\\nIf multiple users or concurrent sessions exist:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Unequal resource allocation:**\\n   - Cannot accurately track token usage per session\\n   - Leads to some sessions consuming excessive resources\\n\\n2. **Service quality degradation:**\\n   - Some sessions may respond slowly due to resource exhaustion\\n   - Affects overall user experience\\n\\n3. **Quota management difficult to implement:**\\n   - Cannot fairly allocate token quotas\\n   - May lead to certain users monopolizing resources\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Problem Severity Assessment\\n\\n| Issue | Severity | Affected Scope | Probability |\\n|-------|----------|----------------|-------------|\\n| Context window overflow | 🔴 High | All long conversations | High |\\n| Conversation management failure | 🟡 Medium | LCM users | Medium |\\n| Cost monitoring failure | 🟡 Medium | All users | High |\\n| LCM function abnormality | 🔴 High | LCM users | High |\\n| User experience degradation | 🟢 Low | All users | High |\\n| Diagnosis difficulty | 🟡 Medium | Developers/Advanced users | Medium |\\n| Resource allocation issues | 🟡 Medium | Multi-user scenarios | Medium |\\n\\n**Overall Severity: 🔴 High**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Case Study 1: Long Conversation Leading to Content Loss\\n\\n**User Scenario:**\\n- Conducting a 50+ turn technical discussion\\n- OpenClaw Display: `0/80k (0%)`\\n- Actual llama-server Usage: `65000/80000 (81%)`\\n\\n**Result:**\\n- User thought there was still ample context available\\n- Continued conversation until model started truncating early content\\n- Key information from technical discussion was forgotten\\n- Conversation quality deteriorated rapidly\\n\\n### Case Study 2: LCM Compression Mechanism Failure\\n\\n**User Scenario:**\\n- Configured automatic compression of historical messages\\n- Expected compression to trigger when token usage reached 70%\\n\\n**Result:**\\n- Due to count being 0, compression never triggered\\n- Historical messages accumulated infinitely\\n- Eventually led to excessive memory usage and slow system response\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Code Location\\n\\n**File:** `~/.npm-global/lib/node_modules/openclaw/dist/pi-embedded-CwMQzdKD.js`\\n**Line:** ~181675 (exact line may vary by version)\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Test Steps\\n\\n1. Compatible (OpenAI format) |\\n| ✅ **OpenAI API** | NOT AFFECTED | Compatible (OpenAI format) |\\n\\n### Root Cause\\n\\nOpenClaw expects these field names at line ~181675:\\n\\n```javascript\\ninput: response.usage?.input_tokens ?? 0,\\noutput: response.usage?.output_tokens ?? 0,\\n```\\n\\nHowever, different frameworks return different field names:\\n\\n#### llama.cpp server (OpenAI-compatible format)\\n```json\\n{\\n  \\\"usage\\\": {\\n    \\\"prompt_tokens\\\": 11,\\n    \\\"completion_tokens\\\": 1,\\n    \\\"total_tokens\\\": 12\\n  }\\n}\\n```\\n\\n#### Ollama (custom format)\\n```json\\n{\\n  \\\"prompt_eval_count\\\": 26,\\n  \\\"eval_count\\\": 259\\n}\\n```\\n\\n#### vLLM / TGI / OpenAI (OpenAI standard format)\\n```json\\n{\\n  \\\"usage\\\": {\\n    \\\"prompt_tokens\\\": 100,\\n    \\\"completion_tokens\\\": 50,\\n    \\\"total_tokens\\\": 150\\n  }\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### Real-World Case\\n\\n**User Configuration:**\\n- OpenClaw Display: `0/80k (0%)`\\n- Remote llama-server (192.168.3.77:8080) Actual Usage: `43250/80000 (54%)`\\n\\n**Cause:** llama.cpp server returns `prompt_tokens`, but OpenClaw expects `input_tokens`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Chain Reactions from Failed Context Statistics\\n\\n### 1. Context Window Overflow Risk\\n\\n**Due to inability to accurately track token usage:**\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n1. User cannot see real-time token usage rate\\n2. Cannot determine if conversation is approaching the 80k context limit\\n3. May lead to:\\n   - **Model truncation:** Ultra-long conversations are forcibly truncated\\n   - **Quality degradation:** Context overflow causes model to forget early conversation\\n   - **Session crash:** API returns errors after exceeding limits\\n\\n**Actual Impact:**\\n- In long conversation scenarios, users may encounter context overflow without warning\\n- Important conversation content may be lost\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 2. Conversation Management Failure\\n\\nOpenClaw's conversation management mechanisms rely on accurate token counting:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Auto-compression mechanism fails:**\\n   - OpenClaw may decide to compress historical messages based on token usage rate\\n   - If count is 0, compression never triggers\\n   - Leads to unlimited accumulation of historical messages, eventually causing memory overflow\\n\\n2. **Session reset strategy fails:**\\n   - Under some configurations, sessions automatically reset when token usage reaches a threshold\\n   - Due to count being 0, reset never triggers\\n   - Leads to uncontrolled session length\\n\\n3. **Resource waste:**\\n   - Cannot accurately evaluate token cost per session\\n   - May lead to unnecessary long conversations\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 3. Cost Monitoring Failure\\n\\nEven with free local models, token statistics are important performance metrics:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Performance analysis difficulty:**\\n   - Cannot analyze token consumption across different conversations\\n   - Cannot identify abnormally high token usage patterns\\n   - Difficult to optimize conversation strategies\\n\\n2. **Multi-model comparison fails:**\\n   - If multiple model backends exist, cannot fairly compare token efficiency\\n   - Cannot make model switching decisions based on token usage\\n\\n3. **API quota monitoring fails** (if using paid APIs):\\n   - Cannot accurately track API quota usage\\n   - May unexpectedly exceed quota causing service interruption\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 4. LCM (Lossless Context Management) Function Abnormalities\\n\\nOpenClaw's LCM system relies on token statistics to manage conversation history:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Historical message compression strategy fails:**\\n   - LCM decides whether to compress history based on token usage rate\\n   - When count is 0, compression never triggers\\n   - Leads to uncontrolled memory usage\\n\\n2. **Context optimization fails:**\\n   - LCM cannot intelligently retain important conversations\\n   - May lead to important information being discarded too early\\n\\n3. **Search and retrieval functionality affected:**\\n   - LCM's search function may rely on token statistics\\n   - Leads to inaccurate search results\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 5. User Experience Degradation\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **User confusion:**\\n   - See `0/80k (0%)` display\\n   - User cannot determine conversation status\\n   - May mistakenly think system is malfunctioning\\n\\n2. **Trust reduction:**\\n   - Key metrics display incorrectly\\n   - User may question the reliability of the entire system\\n\\n3. **Cannot optimize conversation strategy:**\\n   - User cannot adjust conversation methods based on token usage\\n   - Cannot learn how to efficiently use the context window\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 6. Diagnosis and Debugging Difficulty\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Problem troubleshooting difficulty:**\\n   - If conversation anomalies occur, cannot locate issues through token statistics\\n   - Increases troubleshooting time costs\\n\\n2. **Performance optimization blocked:**\\n   - Cannot perform performance optimization based on token statistics\\n   - Difficult to identify performance bottlenecks\\n\\n3. **Automated testing fails:**\\n   - Automated tests may rely on token statistics as success metrics\\n   - Leads to inaccurate test results\\n\\n---\\n\\n### 7. Resource Allocation Issues in Multi-User/Multi-Session Scenarios\\n\\nIf multiple users or concurrent sessions exist:\\n\\n**Chain Reactions:**\\n\\n1. **Unequal resource allocation:**\\n   - Cannot accurately track token usage per session\\n   - Leads to some sessions consuming excessive resources\\n\\n2. **Service quality degradation:**\\n   - Some sessions may respond slowly due to resource exhaustion\\n   - Affects overall user experience\\n\\n3. **Quota management difficult to implement:**\\n   - Cannot fairly allocate token quotas\\n   - May lead to certain users monopolizing resources\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Problem Severity Assessment\\n\\n| Issue | Severity | Affected Scope | Probability |\\n|-------|----------|----------------|-------------|\\n| Context window overflow | 🔴 High | All long conversations | High |\\n| Conversation management failure | 🟡 Medium | LCM users | Medium |\\n| Cost monitoring failure | 🟡 Medium | All users | High |\\n| LCM function abnormality | 🔴 High | LCM users | High |\\n| User experience degradation | 🟢 Low | All users | High |\\n| Diagnosis difficulty | 🟡 Medium | Developers/Advanced users | Medium |\\n| Resource allocation issues | 🟡 Medium | Multi-user scenarios | Medium |\\n\\n**Overall Severity: 🔴 High**\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Case Study 1: Long Conversation Leading to Content Loss\\n\\n**User Scenario:**\\n- Conducting a 50+ turn technical discussion\\n- OpenClaw Display: `0/80k (0%)`\\n- Actual llama-server Usage: `65000/80000 (81%)`\\n\\n**Result:**\\n- User thought there was still ample context available\\n- Continued conversation until model started truncating early content\\n- Key information from technical discussion was forgotten\\n- Conversation quality deteriorated rapidly\\n\\n### Case Study 2: LCM Compression Mechanism Failure\\n\\n**User Scenario:**\\n- Configured automatic compression of historical messages\\n- Expected compression to trigger when token usage reached 70%\\n\\n**Result:**\\n- Due to count being 0, compression never triggered\\n- Historical messages accumulated infinitely\\n- Eventually led to excessive memory usage and slow system response\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Code Location\\n\\n**File:** `~/.npm-global/lib/node_modules/openclaw/dist/pi-embedded-CwMQzdKD.js`\\n**Line:** ~181675 (exact line may vary by version)\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Test Steps\\n\\n1. /Users/aikoorhon/Library/Messages/Attachments/df/15/0449D7CE-A973-4444-BAD7-514214D5F00A/IMG_3719.png\\n```\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nThe `image` tool validates paths via `assertLocalMediaAllowed` using roots from `getAgentScopedMediaLocalRoots`, which only includes:\\n- System temp dir\\n- `~/.openclaw/media/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/agents/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/workspace/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/sandboxes/`\\n- Agent workspace (e.g. `~/clawd/`)\\n\\n`~/Library/Messages/Attachments` is not in any of these.\\n\\nThe iMessage channel has its own separate `attachmentRoots` config (default: `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`) that correctly validates inbound attachments — but those roots are **not passed through** to the image tool's `localRoots` parameter. The two security checks are disconnected.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure iMessage channel with `includeAttachments: true`\\n2. Send an image via iMessage\\n3. Call the `image` tool with the path from the inbound message metadata\\n4. → `LocalMediaAccessError: path-not-allowed`\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\nThe iMessage channel's `attachmentRoots` should be merged into `mediaLocalRoots` when dispatching to the agent, so the `image` tool can read inbound attachments from their native Messages paths. This worked before 2026.3.2.\\n\\n## Config\\n\\n```json\\nchannels.imessage.includeAttachments: true\\n```\\nNo explicit `attachmentRoots` set (using default `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`).\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\nIn the iMessage inbound dispatch path, merge `attachmentRoots` into the `mediaLocalRoots` passed to the tool execution context — similar to how other channels handle scoped media type\\n\\nCrash (process/app exits or hangs)\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` fails to detect orphaned tool IDs produced by MiniMax (and other OpenAI-compat models) because the repair function operates on raw JSONL IDs, while the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from those IDs before sending to the API. The two ID spaces never match, so the repair passes cleanly while the API still rejects with 400.\\n\\nThis is a distinct regression from the fix in #13799 (`sanitizeToolCallIds`). That fix sanitizes IDs at serialization time, but `repairToolUseResultPairing` runs on the pre-sanitization JSONL and does its pairing check against the original IDs — so it never sees the mismatch.\\n\\n### Steps to reproduce\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\n### Step 1 — Mixed-model session\\n\\nThe session uses `haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5` for heartbeat turns and `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6` as the main model. MiniMax generates tool call IDs in the format:\\n\\n\\u003e call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1\\n\\nThese are persisted to the session JSONL verbatim.\\n\\n### Step 2 — Underscore-stripping during Anthropic serialization\\n\\nWhen OpenClaw serializes session history for the Anthropic API, tool IDs are normalized (underscores stripped). The JSONL ID `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` becomes `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the final payload.\\n\\n### Step 3 — Repair function operates on JSONL IDs, not serialized IDs\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` builds its pairing maps from raw JSONL content using `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1`. It finds a matching `toolResult` with the same ID in JSONL, concludes the pair is intact, and passes the message through.\\n\\nThe Anthropic API receives `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the `tool_use` block and looks for a matching `tool_result.tool_use_id`. It finds none and returns 400.\\n\\n### Confirmed from session JSONL\\n\\n| JSONL Entry | Role | Model | Tool ID (JSONL) |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| 31 | assistant | minimax/MiniMax-M2.5 | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` |\\n| 32 | toolResult | — | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` ✅ matched in JSONL |\\n| 110 | assistant | claude-sonnet-4-6 | `content: []`, `stopReason: \\\"error\\\"` — session bricked |\\n\\nThe repair function sees entries 31→32 as a valid pair (they match in JSONL). But the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from `tool_use.id` without applying the same normalization to `tool_result.tool_use_id`, so the API sees an unpaired `tool_use` block.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure `agents.defaults.heartbeat.model: \\\"haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\\"` (or any OpenAI-compat model generating `call_function_*`-format IDs)\\n2. Trigger a heartbeat that causes MiniMax to make tool calls (e.g. a clawflows scheduler run)\\n3. Send a message to the main session routing to `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6`\\n4. Observe: Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\nReproduces reliably after ~4 turns.\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\n**Option A (preferred):** Apply the same underscore-stripping normalization inside `repairToolUseResultPairing` when building ID lookup maps, so it operates on the post-sanitization ID space.\\n\\n**Option B:** Apply normalization symmetrically to both `tool_use.id` and `tool_result.tool_use_id` during serialization, so they always match in the final payload.\\n\\n**Option C:** Add a post-serialization validation pass in the Anthropic serializer that checks every `tool_use` block has a matching `tool_result` using the final serialized IDs, injecting a synthetic error result if not.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n### Expected behavior\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` should normalize tool IDs to the same form used during Anthropic API serialization **before** performing pairing validation, so it catches mismatches the API will reject.\\n\\n\\n\\n### Actual behavior\\n\\n Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\n### OpenClaw version\\n\\n2026.3.13\\n\\n### Operating system\\n\\nLinux 6.6.87.2-microsoft-standard-WSL2 (x64)\\n\\n### Install method\\n\\nnpm global\\n\\n### Model\\n\\nminimax/MiniMax-M2.5 (heartbeat) and anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6 (primary model)\\n\\n### Provider / routing chain\\n\\nhaimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\n\\n### Additional provider/model setup details\\n\\n_No response_\\n\\n### Logs, screenshots, and evidence\\n\\n```shell\\n\\n```\\n\\n### Impact and severity\\n\\nAfter as few as four turns, session context is lost because the only way to recover is to start a new session with the /new command. OpenClaw often hasn't completed (and is no longer able to) complete updating .md files, skills, memory, and long term context. \\n\\n### Additional information\\n\\n## Related\\n\\n- #13799 (closed) — repairToolUseResultPairing misses orphaned tool IDs from MiniMax/OpenAI-compat models — underscore-stripping creates ID mismatch between JSONL and Anthropic API payload\",\"body\":\"### Bug type\\n\\nCrash (process/app exits or hangs)\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` fails to detect orphaned tool IDs produced by MiniMax (and other OpenAI-compat models) because the repair function operates on raw JSONL IDs, while the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from those IDs before sending to the API. The two ID spaces never match, so the repair passes cleanly while the API still rejects with 400.\\n\\nThis is a distinct regression from the fix in #13799 (`sanitizeToolCallIds`). That fix sanitizes IDs at serialization time, but `repairToolUseResultPairing` runs on the pre-sanitization JSONL and does its pairing check against the original IDs — so it never sees the mismatch.\\n\\n### Steps to reproduce\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\n### Step 1 — Mixed-model session\\n\\nThe session uses `haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5` for heartbeat turns and `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6` as the main model. MiniMax generates tool call IDs in the format:\\n\\n\\u003e call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1\\n\\nThese are persisted to the session JSONL verbatim.\\n\\n### Step 2 — Underscore-stripping during Anthropic serialization\\n\\nWhen OpenClaw serializes session history for the Anthropic API, tool IDs are normalized (underscores stripped). The JSONL ID `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` becomes `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the final payload.\\n\\n### Step 3 — Repair function operates on JSONL IDs, not serialized IDs\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` builds its pairing maps from raw JSONL content using `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1`. It finds a matching `toolResult` with the same ID in JSONL, concludes the pair is intact, and passes the message through.\\n\\nThe Anthropic API receives `callfunction0mtm97w4iryj1` in the `tool_use` block and looks for a matching `tool_result.tool_use_id`. It finds none and returns 400.\\n\\n### Confirmed from session JSONL\\n\\n| JSONL Entry | Role | Model | Tool ID (JSONL) |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| 31 | assistant | minimax/MiniMax-M2.5 | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` |\\n| 32 | toolResult | — | `call_function_0mtm97w4iryj_1` ✅ matched in JSONL |\\n| 110 | assistant | claude-sonnet-4-6 | `content: []`, `stopReason: \\\"error\\\"` — session bricked |\\n\\nThe repair function sees entries 31→32 as a valid pair (they match in JSONL). But the Anthropic serializer strips underscores from `tool_use.id` without applying the same normalization to `tool_result.tool_use_id`, so the API sees an unpaired `tool_use` block.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure `agents.defaults.heartbeat.model: \\\"haimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\\"` (or any OpenAI-compat model generating `call_function_*`-format IDs)\\n2. Trigger a heartbeat that causes MiniMax to make tool calls (e.g. a clawflows scheduler run)\\n3. Send a message to the main session routing to `anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6`\\n4. Observe: Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\nReproduces reliably after ~4 turns.\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\n**Option A (preferred):** Apply the same underscore-stripping normalization inside `repairToolUseResultPairing` when building ID lookup maps, so it operates on the post-sanitization ID space.\\n\\n**Option B:** Apply normalization symmetrically to both `tool_use.id` and `tool_result.tool_use_id` during serialization, so they always match in the final payload.\\n\\n**Option C:** Add a post-serialization validation pass in the Anthropic serializer that checks every `tool_use` block has a matching `tool_result` using the final serialized IDs, injecting a synthetic error result if not.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n### Expected behavior\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\n`repairToolUseResultPairing` should normalize tool IDs to the same form used during Anthropic API serialization **before** performing pairing validation, so it catches mismatches the API will reject.\\n\\n\\n\\n### Actual behavior\\n\\n Anthropic returns 400 `messages.N: tool_use ids were found without tool_result blocks immediately after: callfunction...`\\n\\n### OpenClaw version\\n\\n2026.3.13\\n\\n### Operating system\\n\\nLinux 6.6.87.2-microsoft-standard-WSL2 (x64)\\n\\n### Install method\\n\\nnpm global\\n\\n### Model\\n\\nminimax/MiniMax-M2.5 (heartbeat) and anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6 (primary model)\\n\\n### Provider / routing chain\\n\\nhaimaker/minimax/MiniMax-M2.5\\n\\n### Additional provider/model setup details\\n\\n_No response_\\n\\n### Logs, screenshots, and evidence\\n\\n```shell\\n\\n```\\n\\n### Impact and severity\\n\\nAfter as few as four turns, session context is lost because the only way to recover is to start a new session with the /new command. OpenClaw often hasn't completed (and is no longer able to) complete updating .md files, skills, memory, and long term context. \\n\\n### Additional information\\n\\n## Related\\n\\n- #13799 (closed) — `sanitizeToolCallIds` excludes Anthropic; prior fix addressed serialization but did not update `repairToolUseResultPairing` to use the same normalized ID space\\n- #37834 — orphaned tool_use fails and the script never runs.\\n\\nSometimes I also see:\\n\\nexec host not allowed (requested gateway; configure tools.exec.host=sandbox to allow)\\nwhich suggests there is also a tools.exec.host macOS/Linux that seems natural.\\nOn Windows, cron+exec feels unreliable because:\\n\\ncommands are rewritten with cd ~\\\\clawd...,\\nexec host not allowed sometimes blocks host execution,\\nand System is spammed with the failing Exec logs.\\nWhat would help\\nFrom a Windows user’s perspective, a few things would make cron+exec much more usable:\\n\\nDon’t inject cd ~\\\\... when the cron payload already has an absolute path (especially on Windows).\\nLet the user decide the working directory via the command itself.\\n\\nClarify and/or provide a recommended configuration for Request\\n\\n  Please investigate whether:\\n\\n  1. via google-antigravity provider) has extremely strict JSON Schema validation for tool/function calling, causing repeated failures (400 \\\"format\\\" errors) with tool schemas that work fine on other providers (Anthropic, OpenAI, etc.).\\n\\n  Impact\\n\\n  - Tool calling with google-antigravity/claude-* models frequently fails with JSON Schema validation errors\\n  - Users see repetitive \\\"format\\\" failures (80+ errors in my usage stats)\\n  - Forces users to use different providers as primary fallbacks\\n\\n  Root Cause\\n\\n  The Cloud Code Assist API rejects a large subset of standard JSON Schema keywords that are used by tool libraries and other LLM providers:\\n\\n  Completely Rejected:\\n  - Structure defs: $ref, $defs, definitions, $schema, $id, patternProperties, additionalProperties, examples\\n\\n  Validation Constraints (strict - cause 400 on any match):\\n  - minLength, maxLength, minimum, maximum, multipleOf, pattern, format\\n  - minItems, maxItems, uniqueItems\\n  - minProperties, maxProperties\\n\\n  Current Mitigation (in codebase)\\n\\n  The project already has a workaround at src/agents/schema/clean-for-gemini.ts that strips these keywords, but this:\\n  - Loses important validation (e.g., pattern matching, min/max lengths)\\n  - Requires schema modification before provider selection\\n  - Doesn't handle all edge cases\\n\\n  Request\\n\\n  Please investigate whether:\\n\\n  1. This is intentional - Cloud Code Assist is designed for a stricter schema subset and apps must comply\\n  2. A bug on Google's side - The validation should accept more of standard JSON Schema Draft 2020-12\\n  3. A version mismatch - Different models/routes have different schema support\\n  4. A misconfiguration - There's an API flag or header to enable looser validation\\n\\n  Reproduction\\n\\n  Any tool schema using standard validation keywords like:\\n  {\\n    \\\"type\\\": \\\"string\\\",\\n    \\\"minLength\\\": 1,\\n    \\\"pattern\\\": \\\"^[a-z]+$\\\"\\n  }\\n\\n  Causes 400 error through Cloud Code Assist but works on Anthropic/OpenAI \\\"https://api.telegram.org/bot\\u003ctoken\\u003e/sendPhoto\\\" \\\\\\n  -F \\\"chat_id=\\u003cchat_id\\u003e\\\" \\\\\\n  -F \\\"photo=@/path/to/image.png\\\" \\\\\\n  -F
